Values\n 14735→\t\t * greater than zero mean the selector matches the document.\n 14736→\t\t *\n 14737→\t\t * A match is computed according to these rules:\n 14738→\t\t * 1. When {@linkcode DocumentSelector} is an array, compute the match for each contained `DocumentFilter` or language identifier and take the maximum value.\n 14739→\t\t * 2. A string will be desugared to become the `language`-part of a {@linkcode DocumentFilter}, so `\"fooLang\"` is like `{ language: \"fooLang\" }`.\n 14740→\t\t * 3. A {@linkcode DocumentFilter} will be matched against the document by comparing its parts with the document. The following rules apply:\n 14741→\t\t *    1. When the `DocumentFilter` is empty (`{}`) the result is `0`\n 14742→\t\t *    2. When `scheme`, `language`, `pattern`, or `notebook` are defined but one doesn't match, the result is `0`\n 14743→\t\t *    3. Matching against `*` gives a score of `5`, matching via equality or via a glob-pattern gives a score of `10`\n 14744→\t\t *    4. The result is the maximum value of each match\n 14745→\t\t *\n 14746→\t\t * Samples:\n 14747→\t\t * ```js\n 14748→\t\t * // default document from disk (file-scheme)\n 14749→\t\t * doc.uri; //'file:///my/file.js'\n 14750→\t\t * doc.languageId; // 'javascript'\n 14751→\t\t * match('javascript', doc); // 10;\n 14752→\t\t * match({ language: 'javascript' }, doc); // 10;\n 14753→\t\t * match({ language: 'javascript', scheme: 'file' }, doc); // 10;\n 14754→\t\t * match('*', doc); // 5\n 14755→\t\t * match('fooLang', doc); // 0\n 14756→\t\t * match(['fooLang', '*'], doc); // 5\n 14757→\t\t *\n 14758→\t\t * // virtual document, e.g. from git-index\n 14759→\t\t * doc.uri; // 'git:/my/file.js'\n 14760→\t\t * doc.languageId; // 'javascript'\n 14761→\t\t * match('javascript', doc); // 10;\n 14762→\t\t * match({ language: 'javascript', scheme: 'git' }, doc); // 10;\n 14763→\t\t * match('*', doc); // 5\n 14764→\t\t *\n 14765→\t\t * // notebook cell document\n 14766→\t\t * doc.uri; // `vscode-notebook-cell:///my/notebook.ipynb#gl65s2pmha`;\n 14767→\t\t * doc.languageId; // 'python'\n 14768→\t\t * match({ notebookType: 'jupyter-notebook' }, doc) // 10\n 14769→\t\t * match({ notebookType: 'fooNotebook', language: 'python' }, doc) // 0\n 14770→\t\t * match({ language: 'python' }, doc) // 10\n 14771→\t\t * match({ notebookType: '*' }, doc) // 5\n 14772→\t\t * ```\n 14773→\t\t *\n 14774→\t\t * @param selector A document selector.\n 14775→\t\t * @param document A text document.\n 14776→\t\t * @returns A number `>0` when the selector matches and `0` when the selector does not match.\n 14777→\t\t */\n 14778→\t\texport function match(selector: DocumentSelector, document: TextDocument): number;\n 14779→\n 14780→\t\t/**\n 14781→\t\t * An {@link Event} which fires when the global set of diagnostics changes. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01FkHawUkdv6sa7fHhkHLYcP","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_011AdJ4KrRogNV8ghNatiHss","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# VS Code Diagnostic API Reference\n\n## Overview\n\nThe Diagnostic API allows VS Code extensions to report code issues (errors, warnings, information, hints) to users within the editor. Diagnostics are language-agnostic markers that represent problems in code, such as compilation errors, linting warnings, or code style suggestions.\n\nDiagnostics are managed through **DiagnosticCollection**, which serves as a container for organizing diagnostics by resource (file URI). The API provides methods to create, update, retrieve, and listen for changes in diagnostics across the editor.\n\nKey features:\n- Report multiple severity levels (Error, Warning, Information, Hint)\n- Organize diagnostics by language or tool source\n- Include related information to help users understand issues\n- Tag diagnostics as deprecated or unnecessary\n- Listen to global diagnostic changes\n- Manage diagnostic lifecycles with proper cleanup\n\n---\n\n## Core Types\n\n### DiagnosticSeverity\n\nEnum representing the severity level of a diagnostic.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport enum DiagnosticSeverity {\n    Error = 0,\n    Warning = 1,\n    Information = 2,\n    Hint = 3\n}\n```\n\n**Values:**\n\n| Value | Numeric | Description |\n|-------|---------|-------------|\n| `Error` | 0 | Something not allowed by the rules of a language or other means. Displayed with red squiggle underline. |\n| `Warning` | 1 | Something suspicious but allowed. Displayed with orange squiggle underline. |\n| `Information` | 2 | Something to inform about but not a problem. Displayed with blue squiggle underline. |\n| `Hint` | 3 | Something to hint to a better way of doing it, like proposing a refactoring. Displayed as subtle dots. |\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- `Error` is the default severity when creating a Diagnostic without specifying severity\n- Severity levels are ordered by importance: Error > Warning > Information > Hint\n- The Problems panel filters and sorts diagnostics by severity\n- The severity level affects UI rendering, gutter icon colors, and minimap coloring\n\n---\n\n### DiagnosticTag\n\nEnum representing additional metadata about the type of a diagnostic.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport enum DiagnosticTag {\n    Unnecessary = 1,\n    Deprecated = 2\n}\n```\n\n**Values:**\n\n| Value | Numeric | Description |\n|-------|---------|-------------|\n| `Unnecessary` | 1 | Unused or unnecessary code. Rendered with reduced opacity (controlled by `editorUnnecessaryCode.opacity` theme color, e.g., 75% opacity). In high contrast themes, uses `editorUnnecessaryCode.border` to underline the code instead of fading. |\n| `Deprecated` | 2 | Deprecated or obsolete code. Rendered with a strike-through line. |\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Tags are optional and can be combined (multiple tags per diagnostic)\n- Tags provide visual feedback without requiring code action integration\n- `Unnecessary` is commonly used for unused variables, imports, or dead code\n- `Deprecated` is commonly used for obsoleted API usage\n- Tags affect rendering only; they don't change severity or classification\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n    range,\n    'Unused variable',\n    vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Information\n);\ndiagnostic.tags = [vscode.DiagnosticTag.Unnecessary];\n```\n\n---\n\n### DiagnosticRelatedInformation\n\nClass representing additional context for a diagnostic, such as related code locations that contribute to the issue.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport class DiagnosticRelatedInformation {\n    location: Location;\n    message: string;\n\n    constructor(location: Location, message: string);\n}\n```\n\n**Properties:**\n\n| Property | Type | Description |\n|----------|------|-------------|\n| `location` | `Location` | The location of this related diagnostic information. A `Location` consists of a `Uri` and a `Range`. |\n| `message` | `string` | The message describing the related information. Should be concise and contextual. |\n\n**Constructor:**\n- **Parameters:**\n  - `location: Location` - The location to reference (required)\n  - `message: string` - Description of the related information (required)\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Used to point to code locations that cause or relate to a diagnostic\n- Commonly used when multiple symbols have the same name (name collision in scope)\n- All related information appears in the Problems panel when you click on a diagnostic\n- Helpful for understanding the context and root cause of issues\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n    range,\n    'Duplicate symbol definition',\n    vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error\n);\n\ndiagnostic.relatedInformation = [\n    new vscode.DiagnosticRelatedInformation(\n        new vscode.Location(firstDefUri, firstDefRange),\n        'First definition here'\n    ),\n    new vscode.DiagnosticRelatedInformation(\n        new vscode.Location(secondDefUri, secondDefRange),\n        'Conflicting definition here'\n    )\n];\n```\n\n---\n\n### Diagnostic\n\nClass representing a single diagnostic (error, warning, info, or hint).\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport class Diagnostic {\n    range: Range;\n    message: string;\n    severity: DiagnosticSeverity;\n    source?: string;\n    code?: string | number | { value: string | number; target: Uri };\n    relatedInformation?: DiagnosticRelatedInformation[];\n    tags?: DiagnosticTag[];\n\n    constructor(\n        range: Range,\n        message: string,\n        severity?: DiagnosticSeverity\n    );\n}\n```\n\n**Properties:**\n\n| Property | Type | Required | Description |\n|----------|------|----------|-------------|\n| `range` | `Range` | Yes | The range in the document to which this diagnostic applies. A `Range` consists of a start and end `Position`. |\n| `message` | `string` | Yes | The human-readable message describing the issue. Should be clear and actionable. |\n| `severity` | `DiagnosticSeverity` | No | The severity level (Error, Warning, Information, Hint). Defaults to `DiagnosticSeverity.Error`. |\n| `source` | `string` | No | The source identifier (e.g., 'typescript', 'eslint', 'pylint'). Displayed in the Problems panel to identify the diagnostic source. |\n| `code` | `string \\| number \\| object` | No | A code or identifier for this diagnostic. Can be a simple string/number or an object with `value` and `target` properties. Used for code actions and quick fixes. |\n| `relatedInformation` | `DiagnosticRelatedInformation[]` | No | Array of related diagnostic information pointing to related code locations. Optional but valuable for complex issues. |\n| `tags` | `DiagnosticTag[]` | No | Array of tags providing additional metadata (Unnecessary, Deprecated). Multiple tags can be applied to a single diagnostic. |\n\n**Constructor:**\n- **Parameters:**\n  - `range: Range` - The affected range (required)\n  - `message: string` - The human-readable message (required)\n  - `severity?: DiagnosticSeverity` - The severity level (optional, defaults to Error)\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Diagnostics are immutable once published in a DiagnosticCollection\n- The range defines where the diagnostic is displayed in the editor (squiggle underline, gutter icon, etc.)\n- Diagnostics are scoped to a specific file URI and collection\n- Only one range per diagnostic; if multiple ranges need highlighting, create multiple diagnostics\n- The `code` property is essential for code action providers to reference diagnostics\n- Messages should be localized for international users\n- Diagnostics are sent to the Problems panel and displayed with minimap icons\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst range = new vscode.Range(\n    new vscode.Position(5, 0),\n    new vscode.Position(5, 10)\n);\n\nconst diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n    range,\n    'Variable is never used',\n    vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning\n);\n\ndiagnostic.source = 'eslint';\ndiagnostic.code = 'no-unused-vars';\ndiagnostic.tags = [vscode.DiagnosticTag.Unnecessary];\n```\n\n---\n\n### DiagnosticChangeEvent\n\nInterface representing the event data when diagnostics change globally.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport interface DiagnosticChangeEvent {\n    readonly uris: readonly Uri[];\n}\n```\n\n**Properties:**\n\n| Property | Type | Description |\n|----------|------|-------------|\n| `uris` | `readonly Uri[]` | An array of resource URIs for which diagnostics have changed. These are file paths where diagnostics were added, modified, or removed. |\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Contains only the URIs that changed (not all URIs in the workspace)\n- Fired when any extension changes diagnostics, not just the current extension\n- Used to refresh UI components that display diagnostics\n- The array is immutable and read-only\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nvscode.languages.onDidChangeDiagnostics(event => {\n    console.log('Diagnostics changed for:', event.uris);\n    // Refresh custom diagnostic display or perform cleanup\n});\n```\n\n---\n\n### DiagnosticCollection\n\nInterface representing a container for managing diagnostics across documents.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport interface DiagnosticCollection extends Iterable<[uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[]]> {\n    readonly name: string;\n\n    set(uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined): void;\n    set(entries: ReadonlyArray<[Uri, readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined]>): void;\n\n    delete(uri: Uri): void;\n    clear(): void;\n\n    forEach(\n        callback: (uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[], collection: DiagnosticCollection) => any,\n        thisArg?: any\n    ): void;\n\n    get(uri: Uri): readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined;\n    has(uri: Uri): boolean;\n\n    dispose(): void;\n}\n```\n\n**Properties:**\n\n| Property | Type | Description |\n|----------|------|-------------|\n| `name` | `string` (readonly) | The name of this diagnostic collection (e.g., 'typescript', 'eslint'). Displayed in the Problems panel and used by task framework for problem matchers. |\n\n**Methods:**\n\n#### set(uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined): void\n\nAssigns or updates diagnostics for a given resource. Replaces existing diagnostics for that resource.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `uri: Uri` - The file URI for which to set diagnostics\n- `diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined` - Array of diagnostics, or `undefined` to clear diagnostics for this URI\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Passing `undefined` clears all diagnostics for the URI (equivalent to `delete()`)\n- Replaces all previous diagnostics for the URI with the new array\n- Empty array `[]` also clears diagnostics for the URI\n- Fires the `onDidChangeDiagnostics` event asynchronously\n- Multiple diagnostics can target the same range\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst uri = vscode.window.activeTextEditor?.document.uri;\nif (uri) {\n    const diagnostics = [\n        new vscode.Diagnostic(range1, 'Error 1', vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error),\n        new vscode.Diagnostic(range2, 'Error 2', vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning)\n    ];\n    collection.set(uri, diagnostics);\n}\n```\n\n#### set(entries: ReadonlyArray<[Uri, readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined]>): void\n\nBatch update for multiple resources in a single call.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `entries: ReadonlyArray<[Uri, readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined]>` - Array of tuples mapping URIs to diagnostic arrays\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Merges multiple tuples with the same URI (e.g., `[[file1, [d1]], [file1, [d2]]]` becomes `[[file1, [d1, d2]]]`)\n- If the same URI appears with `undefined` after diagnostics, all previous diagnostics are removed before adding subsequent ones\n- More efficient than calling `set()` multiple times\n- Fires a single `onDidChangeDiagnostics` event for all changes\n- Allows atomic updates across multiple files\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\ncollection.set([\n    [uri1, [diagnostic1, diagnostic2]],\n    [uri2, [diagnostic3]],\n    [uri3, undefined]  // Clears diagnostics for uri3\n]);\n```\n\n#### delete(uri: Uri): void\n\nRemoves all diagnostics for the specified URI.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `uri: Uri` - The file URI for which to remove diagnostics\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Equivalent to `set(uri, undefined)`\n- Fires the `onDidChangeDiagnostics` event\n- No-op if the URI has no diagnostics\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\ncollection.delete(uri);\n```\n\n#### clear(): void\n\nRemoves all diagnostics from this collection.\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Equivalent to calling `delete()` on every URI that has diagnostics\n- Fires the `onDidChangeDiagnostics` event once\n- Used during extension cleanup or when reloading diagnostics\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\ncollection.clear();\n```\n\n#### forEach(callback, thisArg?): void\n\nIterates over each URI and its diagnostics in the collection.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `callback: (uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[], collection: DiagnosticCollection) => any` - Function to execute for each entry\n- `thisArg?: any` - Optional context for the callback function\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Iteration order is implementation-dependent\n- Diagnostics array is immutable (read-only)\n- Modifying the collection during iteration is safe; iteration continues with the snapshot taken at call time\n- Useful for custom reporting or cleanup\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\ncollection.forEach((uri, diagnostics, collection) => {\n    console.log(`File: ${uri.fsPath}, Issues: ${diagnostics.length}`);\n});\n```\n\n#### get(uri: Uri): readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined\n\nRetrieves diagnostics for a given resource.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `uri: Uri` - The file URI\n\n**Returns:**\n- `readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined` - Immutable array of diagnostics, or `undefined` if no diagnostics exist for the URI\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Returns `undefined` if the URI has no diagnostics (not an empty array)\n- The returned array is immutable; modifications will not affect the collection\n- Safe to cache the reference; it won't change between calls for the same URI\n- Used to check for existing diagnostics before updating\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst diagnostics = collection.get(uri);\nif (diagnostics) {\n    console.log(`Found ${diagnostics.length} issues`);\n}\n```\n\n#### has(uri: Uri): boolean\n\nChecks if the collection contains diagnostics for a given resource.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `uri: Uri` - The file URI\n\n**Returns:**\n- `boolean` - `true` if the collection has diagnostics for the URI, `false` otherwise\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Faster than checking if `get(uri)` returns `undefined`\n- Useful for conditional logic\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nif (collection.has(uri)) {\n    // URI has diagnostics\n}\n```\n\n#### dispose(): void\n\nCleans up the collection and releases associated resources.\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Calls `clear()` before disposing\n- After disposal, the collection should not be used\n- Prevents memory leaks when extensions unload\n- Should be called in the extension's deactivation hook\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\ncontext.subscriptions.push(diagnosticsCollection);\n// or manually:\n// extension.deactivate() { diagnosticsCollection.dispose(); }\n```\n\n**Iterable Protocol:**\n\nDiagnosticCollection implements the Iterable protocol, allowing it to be used with `for...of` loops.\n\n```typescript\nfor (const [uri, diagnostics] of collection) {\n    console.log(`${uri.fsPath}: ${diagnostics.length} issues`);\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Functions\n\n### createDiagnosticCollection(name?: string)\n\nFactory function for creating a new diagnostic collection.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport function createDiagnosticCollection(name?: string): DiagnosticCollection\n```\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `name?: string` - Optional name for the collection (e.g., 'typescript', 'eslint', 'my-linter'). If not provided, VS Code generates a name. The name is displayed in the Problems panel and used by the task framework.\n\n**Returns:**\n- `DiagnosticCollection` - A new diagnostic collection instance\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Each call creates a new, independent collection\n- Collection names should be descriptive and match the tool/language identifier\n- Multiple collections can coexist; they don't interfere with each other\n- Collections are owned by the extension; they should be disposed when the extension unloads\n- Extension can create multiple collections for different diagnostic sources\n\n**Error Cases:**\n- No errors are thrown; the function always succeeds\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst typescriptDiagnostics = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('typescript');\nconst lintDiagnostics = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('eslint');\n\n// Use both collections\ntypescriptDiagnostics.set(uri, [typeError]);\nlintDiagnostics.set(uri, [lintWarning]);\n```\n\n---\n\n### getDiagnostics(resource?: Uri)\n\nRetrieves diagnostics for a specific resource or the entire workspace.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport function getDiagnostics(resource: Uri): Diagnostic[];\nexport function getDiagnostics(): [Uri, Diagnostic[]][];\n```\n\n**Overloads:**\n\n#### getDiagnostics(resource: Uri): Diagnostic[]\n\nGets all diagnostics for a specific file.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `resource: Uri` - The file URI\n\n**Returns:**\n- `Diagnostic[]` - Array of all diagnostics from all collections for the specified file, or empty array if none exist\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Returns diagnostics from all diagnostic collections (not just one)\n- Includes diagnostics from all sources (TypeScript, linters, extensions, etc.)\n- Ordered by severity (Error > Warning > Information > Hint)\n- Returns empty array `[]` if no diagnostics exist for the resource\n- Performance is O(total diagnostics); suitable for querying individual files\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst diagnostics = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics(uri);\ndiagnostics.forEach(diag => {\n    console.log(`${diag.severity}: ${diag.message}`);\n});\n```\n\n#### getDiagnostics(): [Uri, Diagnostic[]][]\n\nGets all diagnostics across the entire workspace.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- None\n\n**Returns:**\n- `[Uri, Diagnostic[]][]` - Array of tuples, each containing a file URI and its diagnostics array\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Combines diagnostics from all collections and all files in the workspace\n- Returns empty array `[]` if no diagnostics exist anywhere\n- Performance can be O(n) where n is total number of diagnostics; use with caution on large workspaces\n- Useful for global diagnostic reporting or workspace-wide analysis\n- Each tuple contains a unique URI; same URI doesn't appear multiple times\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst allDiagnostics = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics();\nconst errorCount = allDiagnostics.reduce(\n    (sum, [_, diags]) => sum + diags.filter(d => d.severity === vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error).length,\n    0\n);\nconsole.log(`Total errors: ${errorCount}`);\n```\n\n---\n\n## Events\n\n### onDidChangeDiagnostics\n\nEvent fired when diagnostics change globally in the editor.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport const onDidChangeDiagnostics: Event<DiagnosticChangeEvent>;\n```\n\n**Type:**\n- `Event<DiagnosticChangeEvent>` - Disposable event subscription\n\n**Event Data:**\n- `DiagnosticChangeEvent` with `uris: readonly Uri[]` - URIs for which diagnostics changed\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Fires when **any** extension changes diagnostics, not just the subscribing extension\n- Only reports URIs that changed, not all URIs in the workspace\n- Fired asynchronously after diagnostic changes are applied\n- Multiple diagnostic changes may be batched into a single event\n- Event fires even if the final diagnostic count for a URI is zero (i.e., diagnostics were cleared)\n- Used to update UI, refresh displays, or perform cleanup operations\n\n**Disposal:**\n- Returns a `Disposable` that removes the listener when disposed\n- Can be stored in `context.subscriptions` for automatic cleanup\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst disposable = vscode.languages.onDidChangeDiagnostics(event => {\n    console.log('Diagnostics changed for:', event.uris.map(u => u.fsPath));\n    // Update custom diagnostic display or perform other actions\n});\n\n// Clean up when done\n// disposable.dispose();\n// or add to extension context for automatic cleanup\ncontext.subscriptions.push(disposable);\n```\n\n---\n\n## Usage Examples\n\n### Basic Usage: Creating and Publishing Diagnostics\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n    // Create a diagnostic collection\n    const diagnosticsCollection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('myLinter');\n\n    // On file open or change, analyze and publish diagnostics\n    const activeEditor = vscode.window.activeTextEditor;\n    if (activeEditor) {\n        const diagnostics = analyzeDocument(activeEditor.document);\n        diagnosticsCollection.set(activeEditor.document.uri, diagnostics);\n    }\n\n    // Clean up\n    context.subscriptions.push(diagnosticsCollection);\n}\n\nfunction analyzeDocument(document: vscode.TextDocument): vscode.Diagnostic[] {\n    const diagnostics: vscode.Diagnostic[] = [];\n\n    for (let i = 0; i < document.lineCount; i++) {\n        const line = document.lineAt(i);\n\n        // Example: Flag long lines\n        if (line.text.length > 100) {\n            const range = new vscode.Range(\n                new vscode.Position(i, 80),\n                new vscode.Position(i, line.text.length)\n            );\n\n            const diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n                range,\n                'Line exceeds 80 characters',\n                vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning\n            );\n            diagnostic.source = 'myLinter';\n            diagnostic.code = 'line-too-long';\n\n            diagnostics.push(diagnostic);\n        }\n    }\n\n    return diagnostics;\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### Advanced Example: Complete Linter Extension\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport class LinterExtension {\n    private diagnosticsCollection: vscode.DiagnosticCollection;\n    private statusBar: vscode.StatusBarItem;\n\n    constructor(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n        this.diagnosticsCollection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('advanced-linter');\n\n        // Watch for file changes\n        vscode.workspace.onDidChangeTextDocument(event => {\n            this.lintDocument(event.document);\n        }, undefined, context.subscriptions);\n\n        // Watch for file opens\n        vscode.workspace.onDidOpenTextDocument(document => {\n            this.lintDocument(document);\n        }, undefined, context.subscriptions);\n\n        // Listen for diagnostic changes to update status bar\n        vscode.languages.onDidChangeDiagnostics(event => {\n            this.updateStatusBar();\n        }, undefined, context.subscriptions);\n\n        // Create status bar item\n        this.statusBar = vscode.window.createStatusBarItem(\n            vscode.StatusBarAlignment.Right,\n            100\n        );\n        context.subscriptions.push(this.statusBar);\n\n        // Clean up\n        context.subscriptions.push(this.diagnosticsCollection);\n    }\n\n    private lintDocument(document: vscode.TextDocument): void {\n        if (document.languageId !== 'javascript' && document.languageId !== 'typescript') {\n            return;\n        }\n\n        const diagnostics = this.analyzeDocument(document);\n        this.diagnosticsCollection.set(document.uri, diagnostics);\n    }\n\n    private analyzeDocument(document: vscode.TextDocument): vscode.Diagnostic[] {\n        const diagnostics: vscode.Diagnostic[] = [];\n        const text = document.getText();\n\n        // Check for unused variables\n        const unusedVarPattern = /let\\s+(\\w+)\\s*=/g;\n        let match;\n        while ((match = unusedVarPattern.exec(text)) !== null) {\n            const varName = match[1];\n            if (!text.includes(varName, match.index + match[0].length)) {\n                const range = document.getWordRangeAtOffset(match.index);\n                if (range) {\n                    const diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n                        range,\n                        `Variable '${varName}' is never used`,\n                        vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Hint\n                    );\n                    diagnostic.source = 'advanced-linter';\n                    diagnostic.code = 'unused-variable';\n                    diagnostic.tags = [vscode.DiagnosticTag.Unnecessary];\n                    diagnostics.push(diagnostic);\n                }\n            }\n        }\n\n        // Check for deprecated functions\n        const deprecatedCalls = text.match(/oldFunction\\(/g);\n        if (deprecatedCalls) {\n            const pos = document.positionAt(text.indexOf('oldFunction'));\n            const range = document.getWordRangeAtOffset(document.offsetAt(pos));\n            if (range) {\n                const diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n                    range,\n                    'oldFunction is deprecated, use newFunction instead',\n                    vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning\n                );\n                diagnostic.source = 'advanced-linter';\n                diagnostic.code = {\n                    value: 'deprecated-function',\n                    target: vscode.Uri.parse('https://docs.example.com/migration')\n                };\n                diagnostic.tags = [vscode.DiagnosticTag.Deprecated];\n                diagnostic.relatedInformation = [\n                    new vscode.DiagnosticRelatedInformation(\n                        new vscode.Location(\n                            vscode.Uri.file(vscode.workspace.workspaceFolders?.[0].uri.fsPath + '/lib/new.ts'),\n                            new vscode.Position(0, 0)\n                        ),\n                        'newFunction definition is here'\n                    )\n                ];\n                diagnostics.push(diagnostic);\n            }\n        }\n\n        return diagnostics;\n    }\n\n    private updateStatusBar(): void {\n        const allDiagnostics = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics();\n        const errorCount = allDiagnostics.reduce(\n            (sum, [_, diags]) => sum + diags.filter(d => d.severity === vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error).length,\n            0\n        );\n        const warningCount = allDiagnostics.reduce(\n            (sum, [_, diags]) => sum + diags.filter(d => d.severity === vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning).length,\n            0\n        );\n\n        this.statusBar.text = `$(error) ${errorCount} $(warning) ${warningCount}`;\n        this.statusBar.show();\n    }\n}\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n    new LinterExtension(context);\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### Example: Batch Diagnostic Updates\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport class BatchDiagnosticsUpdater {\n    private diagnosticsCollection: vscode.DiagnosticCollection;\n\n    constructor() {\n        this.diagnosticsCollection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('batch-updater');\n    }\n\n    // Update multiple files at once\n    updateAllFiles(results: Map<vscode.Uri, vscode.Diagnostic[]>): void {\n        const entries: Array<[vscode.Uri, vscode.Diagnostic[]]> = [];\n\n        results.forEach((diagnostics, uri) => {\n            entries.push([uri, diagnostics]);\n        });\n\n        // Single batch update is more efficient than individual set() calls\n        this.diagnosticsCollection.set(entries);\n    }\n\n    // Clear specific files while keeping others\n    clearFiles(uris: vscode.Uri[]): void {\n        const entries: Array<[vscode.Uri, undefined]> = uris.map(uri => [uri, undefined]);\n        this.diagnosticsCollection.set(entries);\n    }\n\n    // Iterate and collect statistics\n    getStatistics(): {\n        fileCount: number;\n        totalIssues: number;\n        errorCount: number;\n        warningCount: number;\n        infoCount: number;\n        hintCount: number;\n    } {\n        let fileCount = 0;\n        let totalIssues = 0;\n        let errorCount = 0;\n        let warningCount = 0;\n        let infoCount = 0;\n        let hintCount = 0;\n\n        this.diagnosticsCollection.forEach((uri, diagnostics) => {\n            fileCount++;\n            totalIssues += diagnostics.length;\n\n            diagnostics.forEach(diag => {\n                switch (diag.severity) {\n                    case vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error:\n                        errorCount++;\n                        break;\n                    case vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning:\n                        warningCount++;\n                        break;\n                    case vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Information:\n                        infoCount++;\n                        break;\n                    case vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Hint:\n                        hintCount++;\n                        break;\n                }\n            });\n        });\n\n        return { fileCount, totalIssues, errorCount, warningCount, infoCount, hintCount };\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### Example: Listening to Diagnostic Changes\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport class DiagnosticListener {\n    constructor(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n        // Listen for changes to any diagnostics in the workspace\n        const disposable = vscode.languages.onDidChangeDiagnostics(event => {\n            this.handleDiagnosticsChanged(event);\n        });\n\n        context.subscriptions.push(disposable);\n    }\n\n    private handleDiagnosticsChanged(event: vscode.DiagnosticChangeEvent): void {\n        console.log('Diagnostics changed for these files:');\n\n        event.uris.forEach(uri => {\n            const diagnostics = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics(uri);\n            console.log(`  ${uri.fsPath}: ${diagnostics.length} issues`);\n\n            // Group by source\n            const bySource = new Map<string | undefined, vscode.Diagnostic[]>();\n            diagnostics.forEach(diag => {\n                if (!bySource.has(diag.source)) {\n                    bySource.set(diag.source, []);\n                }\n                bySource.get(diag.source)!.push(diag);\n            });\n\n            bySource.forEach((diags, source) => {\n                console.log(`    ${source || 'unknown'}: ${diags.length}`);\n            });\n        });\n\n        // You could also perform actions like:\n        // - Refresh a custom diagnostic viewer\n        // - Update a status bar\n        // - Trigger code actions\n        // - Save results to a file\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### Example: Related Information for Symbol Conflicts\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport function reportSymbolConflicts(\n    collection: vscode.DiagnosticCollection,\n    uri: vscode.Uri,\n    symbolDefinitions: Array<{ name: string; range: vscode.Range }[]>\n) {\n    const diagnostics: vscode.Diagnostic[] = [];\n\n    // For each symbol that appears multiple times, create diagnostics with related info\n    symbolDefinitions.forEach((locations, symbolIndex) => {\n        if (locations.length > 1) {\n            // Create a diagnostic for the first location\n            const primary = locations[0];\n            const diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n                primary.range,\n                `Symbol '${primary.name}' is defined multiple times`,\n                vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error\n            );\n            diagnostic.source = 'symbol-checker';\n            diagnostic.code = 'duplicate-symbol';\n\n            // Add related information for other definitions\n            diagnostic.relatedInformation = locations.slice(1).map((location, index) => {\n                return new vscode.DiagnosticRelatedInformation(\n                    new vscode.Location(uri, location.range),\n                    `Also defined here (occurrence ${index + 2})`\n                );\n            });\n\n            diagnostics.push(diagnostic);\n        }\n    });\n\n    collection.set(uri, diagnostics);\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Common Patterns\n\n### Pattern 1: Diagnostic Collection Lifecycle\n\nAlways manage the lifecycle of diagnostic collections:\n\n```typescript\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n    const collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('myExt');\n\n    // Use the collection...\n\n    // Add to context.subscriptions for automatic cleanup on deactivation\n    context.subscriptions.push(collection);\n\n    // Alternatively, manually dispose:\n    // context.subscriptions.push({\n    //     dispose() { collection.dispose(); }\n    // });\n}\n\nexport function deactivate() {\n    // All subscriptions are automatically disposed\n}\n```\n\n### Pattern 2: Filtering Diagnostics\n\n```typescript\n// Get diagnostics of a specific severity\nconst errorDiagnostics = allDiagnostics.filter(\n    d => d.severity === vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error\n);\n\n// Get diagnostics from a specific source\nconst typescriptDiags = allDiagnostics.filter(\n    d => d.source === 'typescript'\n);\n\n// Get diagnostics with specific tags\nconst deprecatedDiags = allDiagnostics.filter(\n    d => d.tags?.includes(vscode.DiagnosticTag.Deprecated)\n);\n\n// Combine filters\nconst unnecessaryWarnings = allDiagnostics.filter(\n    d => d.severity === vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning &&\n         d.tags?.includes(vscode.DiagnosticTag.Unnecessary)\n);\n```\n\n### Pattern 3: Incremental Diagnostic Updates\n\nInstead of clearing and resetting all diagnostics, update only affected files:\n\n```typescript\nexport class IncrementalDiagnosticsUpdater {\n    private diagnosticsCollection: vscode.DiagnosticCollection;\n    private changedFiles = new Set<vscode.Uri>();\n\n    constructor() {\n        this.diagnosticsCollection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('incremental');\n    }\n\n    markFileChanged(uri: vscode.Uri): void {\n        this.changedFiles.add(uri);\n    }\n\n    updateChangedFiles(): void {\n        if (this.changedFiles.size === 0) {\n            return;\n        }\n\n        const entries: Array<[vscode.Uri, vscode.Diagnostic[] | undefined]> = [];\n\n        this.changedFiles.forEach(uri => {\n            const diagnostics = this.analyzefile(uri);\n            entries.push([uri, diagnostics]);\n        });\n\n        // Batch update\n        this.diagnosticsCollection.set(entries);\n        this.changedFiles.clear();\n    }\n\n    private analyzefile(uri: vscode.Uri): vscode.Diagnostic[] {\n        // Analysis logic...\n        return [];\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Pattern 4: Diagnostic Collection per Source\n\nUse separate collections for different diagnostic sources for better organization:\n\n```typescript\nexport class MultiSourceDiagnostics {\n    private linterDiagnostics: vscode.DiagnosticCollection;\n    private typecheckerDiagnostics: vscode.DiagnosticCollection;\n    private customDiagnostics: vscode.DiagnosticCollection;\n\n    constructor(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n        this.linterDiagnostics = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('eslint');\n        this.typecheckerDiagnostics = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('typescript');\n        this.customDiagnostics = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('custom-rules');\n\n        context.subscriptions.push(\n            this.linterDiagnostics,\n            this.typecheckerDiagnostics,\n            this.customDiagnostics\n        );\n    }\n\n    updateLinterIssues(uri: vscode.Uri, diagnostics: vscode.Diagnostic[]): void {\n        this.linterDiagnostics.set(uri, diagnostics);\n    }\n\n    updateTypeIssues(uri: vscode.Uri, diagnostics: vscode.Diagnostic[]): void {\n        this.typecheckerDiagnostics.set(uri, diagnostics);\n    }\n\n    updateCustomIssues(uri: vscode.Uri, diagnostics: vscode.Diagnostic[]): void {\n        this.customDiagnostics.set(uri, diagnostics);\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Pattern 5: Querying and Filtering All Workspace Diagnostics\n\n```typescript\nexport class DiagnosticsAnalyzer {\n    /**\n     * Get all diagnostics of a specific severity across the workspace\n     */\n    static getAllBySeverity(severity: vscode.DiagnosticSeverity): vscode.Diagnostic[] {\n        const allDiagnostics = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics();\n        const filtered: vscode.Diagnostic[] = [];\n\n        allDiagnostics.forEach(([_, diags]) => {\n            diags.forEach(diag => {\n                if (diag.severity === severity) {\n                    filtered.push(diag);\n                }\n            });\n        });\n\n        return filtered;\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Get all diagnostics from a specific source\n     */\n    static allDiagnostics.forEach(([_, diags]) => {\n            diags.forEach(diag => {\n                if (diag.source === source) {\n                    filtered.push(diag);\n                }\n            });\n        });\n\n        return filtered;\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Count diagnostics by severity\n     */\n    static countBySeverity(): Map<string, number> {\n        const counts = new Map<string, number>();\n        const severityNames = ['Error', 'Warning', 'Information', 'Hint'];\n\n        severityNames.forEach(name => counts.set(name, 0));\n\n        const allDiagnostics = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics();\n        allDiagnostics.forEach(([_, diags]) => {\n            diags.forEach(diag => {\n                const severityName = severityNames[diag.severity];\n                counts.set(severityName, (counts.get(severityName) || 0) + 1);\n            });\n        });\n\n        return counts;\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### Common Error Scenarios\n\n#### 1. Using Disposed Collection\n\n**Problem:** Attempting to use a diagnostic collection after `dispose()` has been called.\n\n```typescript\nconst collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('test');\ncollection.dispose();\ncollection.set(uri, diagnostics); // May fail or cause unexpected behavior\n```\n\n**Solution:** Track collection state or ensure proper lifecycle management.\n\n```typescript\nclass SafeDiagnosticsCollection {\n    private disposed = false;\n\n    constructor(private collection: vscode.DiagnosticCollection) {}\n\n    set(uri: vscode.Uri, diagnostics: vscode.Diagnostic[] | undefined): void {\n        if (this.disposed) {\n            throw new Error('Collection has been disposed');\n        }\n        this.collection.set(uri, diagnostics);\n    }\n\n    dispose(): void {\n        this.collection.dispose();\n        this.disposed = true;\n    }\n}\n```\n\n#### 2. Invalid Range in Diagnostic\n\n**Problem:** Creating a diagnostic with an invalid range (e.g., end position before start position).\n\n```typescript\nconst diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n    new vscode.Range(end, start), // Wrong order!\n    'Error message',\n    vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error\n);\n```\n\n**Solution:** Ensure range positions are correctly ordered.\n\n```typescript\nconst start = new vscode.Position(line, startChar);\nconst end = new vscode.Position(line, endChar);\n\nif (start.isBefore(end) || start.isEqual(end)) {\n    const diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n        new vscode.Range(start, end),\n        'Error message',\n        vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error\n    );\n}\n```\n\n#### 3. Out-of-Bounds Range\n\n**Problem:** Range extends beyond document boundaries.\n\n```typescript\n// Document has 50 lines, but we create range at line 100\nconst range = new vscode.Range(100, 0, 101, 0); // Out of bounds\n```\n\n**Solution:** Validate ranges against document bounds.\n\n```typescript\nfunction createDiagnosticSafe(\n    document: vscode.TextDocument,\n    line: number,\n    column: number,\n    message: string\n): vscode.Diagnostic | undefined {\n    if (line < 0 || line >= document.lineCount) {\n        return undefined;\n    }\n\n    const lineLength = document.lineAt(line).text.length;\n    if (column < 0 || column > lineLength) {\n        return undefined;\n    }\n\n    const range = new vscode.Range(line, column, line, Math.min(column + 10, lineLength));\n    return new vscode.Diagnostic(\n        range,\n        message,\n        vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error\n    );\n}\n```\n\n#### 4. Missing or Null URIs\n\n**Problem:** Passing invalid URIs to diagnostic methods.\n\n```typescript\ncollection.set(null, diagnostics); // TypeError\ncollection.set(undefined, diagnostics); // TypeError\n```\n\n**Solution:** Validate URIs before use.\n\n```typescript\nfunction safeDiagnosticSet(\n    collection: vscode.DiagnosticCollection,\n    uri: vscode.Uri | undefined,\n    diagnostics: vscode.Diagnostic[]\n): void {\n    if (!uri) {\n        console.warn('Invalid URI provided to diagnostic set');\n        return;\n    }\n    collection.set(uri, diagnostics);\n}\n```\n\n#### 5. Memory Leaks from Uncleaned Listeners\n\n**Problem:** Creating event listeners without proper cleanup.\n\n```typescript\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n    vscode.languages.onDidChangeDiagnostics(event => {\n        // Listener never cleaned up!\n        handleDiagnosticsChanged(event);\n    });\n}\n```\n\n**Solution:** Always add subscriptions to `context.subscriptions`.\n\n```typescript\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n    const disposable = vscode.languages.onDidChangeDiagnostics(event => {\n        handleDiagnosticsChanged(event);\n    });\n\n    context.subscriptions.push(disposable);\n}\n```\n\n#### 6. Accessing Immutable Arrays\n\n**Problem:** Attempting to modify returned diagnostic arrays.\n\n```typescript\nconst diagnostics = collection.get(uri);\nif (diagnostics) {\n    diagnostics[0].message = 'Changed'; // Type error: read-only\n    diagnostics.push(newDiagnostic); // Type error: read-only\n}\n```\n\n**Solution:** Create a new array for modifications.\n\n```typescript\nconst diagnostics = collection.get(uri);\nif (diagnostics) {\n    const updated = diagnostics.map(d => {\n        if (d.message === 'Old') {\n            const newDiag = new vscode.Diagnostic(d.range, 'New', d.severity);\n            newDiag.source = d.source;\n            return newDiag;\n        }\n        return d;\n    });\n    collection.set(uri, updated);\n}\n```\n\n### Performance Considerations\n\n1. **Batch Updates:** Use `set(entries)` with multiple tuples instead of individual `set()` calls.\n2. **Lazy Evaluation:** Don't compute all diagnostics upfront; update only changed files.\n3. **Event Debouncing:** Debounce rapid diagnostic updates from text document changes.\n4. **Large Workspaces:** Be cautious with `getDiagnostics()` without parameters; it can be slow in large workspaces.\n5. **Memory Management:** Always dispose collections and unsubscribe from events.\n\n---\n\n## Architecture Notes\n\n### Internal Implementation\n\nThe Diagnostic API is built on VS Code's marker system:\n\n1. **Extension Host:** Extensions create `Diagnostic` objects and publish them through `DiagnosticCollection`\n2. **Protocol:** Changes are communicated to the main process via `$changeMany()` and `$clear()` RPC calls\n3. **Marker Service:** Diagnostics are converted to `IMarkerData` and stored in the marker service\n4. **UI Rendering:** The Problems panel, editor gutter, and minimap display markers based on severity and location\n5. **Event Dispatch:** Changes trigger `onDidChangeDiagnostics` event globally\n\n### Disposal Semantics\n\n- When a `DiagnosticCollection` is disposed, it clears all its diagnostics\n- Extensions should dispose collections during deactivation\n- Undisposed collections consume memory and may prevent proper extension cleanup\n\n---\n\n## Best Practices\n\n1. **Use Descriptive Names:** Name collections after their source (e.g., 'typescript', 'eslint', 'my-linter')\n2. **Set Source Property:** Always set the `source` property for diagnostic attribution\n3. **Provide Codes:** Include `code` property for code action integration\n4. **Add Related Info:** Use `relatedInformation` for complex diagnostics\n5. **Apply Tags:** Use tags to categorize diagnostics semantically\n6. **Batch Updates:** Combine multiple updates into a single `set()` call\n7. **Clean Up:** Always dispose collections in extension deactivation\n8. **Validate Input:** Check URI and range validity before creating diagnostics\n9. **Localize Messages:** Use `vscode.l10n` for diagnostic messages\n10. **Document Codes:** Document diagnostic codes for external tool integration\n\n---\n\n## Related APIs\n\n- **CodeActionProvider:** Respond to diagnostics with code fixes\n- **CodeLensProvider:** Show additional information related to diagnostics\n- **Task Framework:** Use diagnostic collection names for problem matchers\n- **Status Bar:** Display diagnostic counts or status\n- **Output Channel:** Log diagnostic processing for
